\\t\\t\\t\\tcontinue\\n54: \\t\\t\\t}\\n55: \\n56: \\t\\t\\t// If both the destination rules are without a workload selector or with matching workload selectors, simply merge them.\\n57: \\t\\t\\t// When computing\\n99: \\t// CDS, we simply have to find the matching service and return the\\n100: \\t// destination rule.\\n101: \\tdestinationRules map[host.Name][]*config.Config\\n102: \\t// OutboundTrafficPolicy defines the outbound traffic policy for this sidecar.\\n103: \\t// If OutboundTrafficPolicy is ALLOW_ANY traffic to unknown destinations will\\n104: \\t// be forwarded.\\n105: \\tOutboundTrafficPolicy *networking.OutboundTrafficPolicy\\n106: \\n107: \\t// Set of known configs this sidecar depends on.\\n108: \\t// This field will be used to determine the config/resource scope\\n109: \\t// which means which config changes will affect the proxies within this scope.\\n110: \\tconfigDependencies map[uint64]struct{}\\n111: \\n112: \\t// The namespace to treat as the administrative root namespace for\\n113: \\t// Istio configuration.\\n114: \\t//\\n115: \\t// Changes to Sidecar resources in this namespace will trigger a push.\\n116: \\tRootNamespace string\\n117: }\\n118: \\n119: // MarshalJSON implements json.Marshaller\\n120: func (sc *SidecarScope) MarshalJSON() ([]byte, error) {\\n121: \\t// Json cannot expose unexported fields, so copy the ones we want here\\n122: \\treturn json.MarshalIndent(map[string]interface{}{\\n123: \\t\\t\\\"version\\\":               sc.Version,\\n124: \\t\\t\\\"rootNamespace\\\":         sc.RootNamespace,\\n125: \\t\\t\\\"name\\\":                  sc.Name,\\n126: \\t\\t\\\"namespace\\\":             sc.Namespace,\\n127: \\t\\t\\\"outboundTrafficPolicy\\\": sc.OutboundTrafficPolicy,\\n128: \\t\\t\\\"services\\\":              sc.services,\\n129: \\t\\t\\\"sidecar\\\":               sc.Sidecar,\\n130: \\t\\t\\\"destinationRules\\\":      sc.destinationRules,\\n131: \\t}, \\\"\\\", \\\"  \\\")\\n132: }\\n133: \\n134: // IstioEgressListenerWrapper is a wrapper for\\n135: // networking.IstioEgressListener object. The wrapper provides performance\\n136: // optimizations as it allows us to precompute and store the list of\\n137: // services/virtualServices that apply to this listener.\\n138: type IstioEgressListenerWrapper struct {\\n139: \\t// The actual IstioEgressListener api object from the Config. It can be\\n140: \\t// nil if this is for the default sidecar scope.\\n141: \\tIstioListener *networking.IstioEgressListener\\n142: \\n143: \\t// List of services imported by this egress listener above.\\n144: \\t// This will be used by LDS and RDS code when\\n145: \\t// building the set of virtual hosts or the tcp filterchain matches for\\n146: \\t// a given listener port. Two listeners, on user specified ports or\\n147: \\t// unix domain sockets could have completely different sets of\\n148: \\t// services. So a global list of services per sidecar scope will be\\n149: \\t// incorrect. Hence the per listener set of services.\\n150: \\tservices []*Service\\n151: \\n152: \\t// List of virtual services imported by this egress listener above.\\n153: \\t// As with per listener services, this\\n154: \\t// will be used by RDS code to compute the virtual host configs for\\n155: \\t// http listeners, as well as by TCP/TLS filter code to compute the\\n156: \\t// service routing configs and the filter chain matches. We need a\\n157: \\t// virtualService set per listener and not one per sidecarScope because\\n158: \\t// each listener imports an independent set of virtual services.\\n159: \\t// Listener 1 could namespace,\\n162: \\t// with a different path rewrite or no path rewrites.\\n163: \\tvirtualServices []config.Config\\n164: \\n165: \\tlistenerHosts map[string][]host.Name\\n166: }\\n167: \\n168: const defaultSidecar = \\\"default-sidecar\\\"\\n169: \\n170: // DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace is a sidecar scope object with a default catch all egress listener\\n171: // that matches the default Istio behavior: a sidecar has listeners for all services in the mesh\\n172: // We use this scope when the user has not set any sidecar Config for a given config namespace.\\n173: func is a wrapper over the Sidecar resource with some\n56: // preprocessed data to determine the list of services, virtualServices,\n57: // and destinationRules that are accessible to a given\n58: // sidecar. Precomputing the list of services, virtual services, dest rules\n59: // for a sidecar improves performance as we no longer need to compute this\n60: // list for every sidecar. We simply have to match a sidecar to a\n61: // SidecarScope. Note that this is not the same as public/private scoped\n62: // services. The list of services seen by every sidecar scope (namespace\n63: // wide or per workload) depends on the imports, the listeners, and other\n64: // settings.\n65: //\n66: // Every proxy workload of SidecarProxy type will always map to a\n67: // SidecarScope object. If the proxy's namespace does not have a user\n68: // specified Sidecar CRD, we will construct one that has a catch all egress\n69: // listener that imports every public service/virtualService in the mesh.\n70: type SidecarScope struct {\n71: \tName string\n72: \t// This is the namespace where the sidecar takes effect,\n73: \t// maybe different from the ns where sidecar resides if sidecar is in root ns.\n74: \tNamespace string\n75: \t// The crd itself. Each hostname in this map\n98: \t// corresponds to a service in the services array above. `p.destRules[resolvedHost]`\n   - When a second DestinationRule is merged, only one rule survives in `p.destRules[resolvedHost]` with the metadata of the first rule\n\n2. **In `sidecar.go`**, the This can be used in\\n40: // places where the type is implied.\\n41: // This is preferred to a ConfigKey with empty Kind, especially in performance sensitive code - hashing this struct\\n42: // is 2x faster than ConfigKey.\\n43: type NamespacedName struct {\\n44: \\tName      string\\n45: \\tNamespace string\\n46: }\\n47: \\n48: func (key NamespacedName) String() string {\\n49: \\treturn key.Namespace + \\\"/\\\" + key.Name\\n50: }\\n51: \\n52: // ConfigKey describe a specific config item.\\n53: // In most cases, the name is the config's name. However, for ServiceEntry it is service's FQDN.\\n54: type ConfigKey struct {\\n55: \\tKind      config.GroupVersionKind\\n56: \\tName      string\\n57: \\tNamespace string\\n58: }\\n59: \\n60: func (key ConfigKey) HashCode() uint64 {\\n61: \\thash := md5.New()\\n62: \\tfor _, v := range []string{\\n63: \\t\\tkey.Name,\\n64: \\t\\tkey.Namespace,\\n65: \\t\\tkey.Kind.Kind,\\n66: \\t\\tkey.Kind.Group,\\n67: \\t\\tkey.Kind.Version,\\n68: \\t} {\\n69: \\t\\thash.Write([]byte(v))\\n70: \\t}\\n71: \\tvar tmp [md5.Size]byte\\n72: \\tsum := hash.Sum(tmp[:0])\\n73: \\treturn binary.BigEndian.Uint64(sum)\\n74: }\\n75: \\n76: func (key ConfigKey) String() string {\\n77: \\treturn key.Kind.Kind + \\\"/\\\" + key.Namespace + \\\"/\\\" + key.Name\\n78: }\\n79: \\n80: // ConfigsOfKind extracts configs of the specified kind.\\n81: func ConfigsOfKind(configs map[ConfigKey]struct{}, kind config.GroupVersionKind) map[ConfigKey]struct{} {\\n82: \\tret := make(map[ConfigKey]struct{})\\n83: \\n84: \\tfor conf := range configs {\\n85: \\t\\tif conf.Kind == kind {\\n86: \\t\\t\\tret[conf] = struct{}{}\\n87: \\t\\t}\\n88: \\t}\\n89: \\n90: \\treturn ret\\n91: }\\n92: \\n93: // ConfigNamesOfKind extracts config names of the specified kind.\\n94: func ConfigNamesOfKind(configs map[ConfigKey]struct{}, kind config.GroupVersionKind) map[string]struct{} {\\n95: \\tret := sets.New()\\n96: \\n97: \\tfor conf := range configs {\\n98: \\t\\tif conf.Kind == kind {\\n99: \\t\\t\\tret.Insert(conf.Name)\\n100: \\t\\t}\\n101: \\t}\\n102: \\n103: \\treturn ret\\n104: }\\n105: \\n106: // ConfigStore describes a set of platform agnostic APIs that must be supported\\n107: // by the underlying platform to store and retrieve Istio configuration.\\n108: //\\n109: // Configuration key is defined to be a combination of the type, name, and\\n110: // namespace of the configuration object. The configuration key is guaranteed\\n111: // to be unique in the store.\\n112: //\\n113: // The storage interface presented here assumes that the underlying storage\\n114: // layer supports _Get_ (list), _Update_ (update), _Create_ (create) and\\n115: // _Delete_ semantics but does not guarantee any transactional semantics.\\n116: //\\n117: // _Update_, _Create_, and _Delete_ are mutator operations. These operations\\n118: // are asynchronous, and you might not see the effect immediately (e.g. _Get_\\n119: // might not return the object by key immediately after you mutate the store.)\\n120: // Intermittent errors might occur even though the operation succeeds, so you\\n121: // should always check if the object store has been modified even if the\\n122: // mutating operation returns an error.  Objects should be created with\\n123: // _Create_ operation and updated with _Update_ operation.\\n124: //\\n125: // Resource versions record the last mutation operation on each object. If a\\n126: // mutation is applied to a different revision of an object than what the\\n127: // underlying storage expects as defined by pure equality, the operation is\\n128: // blocked.  The client of this interface should not make assumptions about the\\n129: // structure or ordering of the revision identifier.\\n130: //\\n131: // Object references supplied and returned from this interface should be\\n132: // treated as read-only. Modifying them violates thread-safety.\\n133: type ConfigStore interface {\\n134: \\t// Schemas exposes the configuration type schema known by the config store.\\n135: \\t// The type schema defines the bidirectional mapping between configuration\\n136: \\t// types and the protobuf encoding schema.\\n137: \\tSchemas() collection.Schemas\\n138: \\n139: \\t// Get retrieves a configuration element by a type and a key\\n140: \\tGet(typ config.GroupVersionKind, name, namespace string) *config.Config\\n141: \\n142: \\t// List returns objects by type and namespace.\\n143: \\t// Use \\\"\\\" for the namespace to list across namespaces.\\n144: \\tList(typ config.GroupVersionKind, namespace string) ([]config.Config, error)\\n145: \\n146: \\t// Create adds a new configuration object to the store. If an object with the\\n147: \\t// same name and namespace for the type already exists, the operation fails\\n148: \\t// with no side effects.\\n149: \\tCreate(config config.Config) (revision string, err error)\\n150: \\n151: \\t// Update modifies an existing configuration object in the store.  Update\\n152: \\t// requires that the object has been created.  Resource version prevents\\n153: \\t// overriding a value that has been changed between prior _Get_ and _Put_\\n154: \\t// operation to achieve optimistic concurrency. This method returns a new\\n155: \\t// revision if the operation succeeds.\\n156: \\tUpdate(config config.Config) (newRevision string, err error)\\n157: \\tUpdateStatus(config config.Config) (newRevision string, err error)\\n158: \\n159: \\t// Patch applies only the modifications made in the PatchFunc rather than doing a full replace. Useful to avoid\\n160: \\t// read-modify-write conflicts when there are many concurrent-writers to the same resource.\\n161: \\tPatch(orig config.Config, patchFn config.PatchFunc) (string, error)\\n162: \\n163: \\t// Delete removes an object from the store by key\\n164: \\t// For k8s, resourceVersion must be fulfilled before a deletion is carried out.\\n165: \\t// If not possible, a 409 Conflict status will be returned.\\n166: \\tDelete(typ config.GroupVersionKind, name, namespace string, resourceVersion *string) error\\n167: }\\n168: \\n169: type EventHandler = func(config.Config, config.Config, Event)\\n170: \\n171: // ConfigStoreCache is a local fully-replicated cache of the config store.  The\\n172: // cache actively synchronizes its local state with the remote store and\\n173: // provides a notification mechanism to receive update events. As such, the\\n174: // notification handlers must be registered prior to calling _Run_, and the\\n175: // cache requires initial synchronization grace period after calling  _Run_.\\n176: //\\n177: // Update notifications require the following consistency guarantee: the view\\n178: // in the cache must be AT LEAST as fresh as the moment notification arrives, but\\n179: // MAY BE more fresh (e.g. if _Delete_ cancels an _Add_ event).\\n180: //\\n181: // Handlers execute on the single worker queue in the order they are appended.\\n182: // Handlers receive the notification event and the associated object. The configuration key is guaranteed\\n111: // to be unique in the store.\\n112: //\\n113: // The storage interface presented here assumes that the underlying storage\\n114: // layer supports _Get_ (list), _Update_ (update), _Create_ (create) and\\n115: // _Delete_ semantics but does not guarantee any transactional semantics.\\n116: //\\n117: // _Update_, _Create_, and _Delete_ are mutator operations. These operations\\n118: // are asynchronous, and you might not see the effect immediately (e.g. _Get_\\n119: // might not return the object by key immediately after you mutate the store.)\\n120: // Intermittent errors might occur even though the operation succeeds, so you\\n121: // should always check if the object store has been modified even if the\\n122: // mutating operation returns an error.  Objects should be created with\\n123: // _Create_ operation and updated with _Update_ operation.\\n124: //\\n125: // Resource versions record the last mutation operation on each object. If a\\n126: // mutation is applied to a different revision of an object than what the\\n127: // underlying storage expects as defined by pure equality, the operation is\\n128: // blocked.  The client of this interface should not make assumptions about the\\n129: // structure or ordering of the revision identifier.\\n130: //\\n131: // Object references supplied and returned from this interface should be\\n132: // treated as read-only. The configuration key is guaranteed\n111: // to be unique in the store.\n112: //\n113: // The storage interface presented here assumes that the underlying storage\n114: // layer supports _Get_ (list), _Update_ (update), _Create_ (create) and\n115: // _Delete_ semantics but does not guarantee any transactional semantics.\n116: //\n117: // _Update_, _Create_, and _Delete_ are mutator operations. These operations\n118: // are asynchronous, and you might not see the effect immediately (e.g. _Get_\n119: // might not return the object by key immediately after you mutate the store.)\n120: // Intermittent errors might occur even though the operation succeeds, so you\n121: // should always check if the object store has been modified even if the\n122: // mutating operation returns an error.  Objects should be created with\n123: // _Create_ operation and updated with _Update_ operation.\n124: //\n125: // Resource versions record the last mutation operation on each object. If a\n126: // mutation is applied to a different revision of an object than what the\n127: // underlying storage expects as defined by pure equality, the operation is\n128: // blocked.  The client of this interface should not make assumptions about the\n129: // structure or ordering of the revision identifier.\n130: //\n131: // Object references supplied and returned from this interface should be\n132: // treated as read-only. Modifying them violates thread-safety.\n133: type ConfigStore interface {\n134: \t// Schemas exposes the configuration type schema known by the config store.\n135: \t// The type schema defines the bidirectional mapping between configuration\n136: \t// types and the protobuf encoding schema.\n137: \tSchemas() collection.Schemas\n138: \n139: \t// Get retrieves a configuration element by a type and a key\n140: \tGet(typ config.GroupVersionKind, name, namespace string) *config.Config\n141: \n142: \t// List returns objects by type and namespace.\n143: \t// Use \"\" for the namespace to list across namespaces.\n144: \tList(typ config.GroupVersionKind, namespace string) ([]config.Config, error)\n145: \n146: \t// Create adds a new configuration object to the store. If an object with the\n147: \t// same name and namespace for the type already exists, the operation fails\n148: \t// with no side effects.\n149: \tCreate(config config.Config) (revision string, err error)\n150: \n151: \t// Update modifies an existing configuration object in the store.  Update\n152: \t// requires that the object has been created.  Resource version prevents\n153: \t// overriding a value that has been changed between prior _Get_ and _Put_\n154: \t// operation to achieve optimistic concurrency. This method returns a new\n155: \t// revision if the operation succeeds.\n156: \tUpdate(config config.Config) (newRevision string, err error)\n157: \tUpdateStatus(config config.Config) (newRevision string, err error)\n158: \n159: \t// Patch applies only the modifications made in the PatchFunc rather than doing a full replace. Useful to avoid\n160: \t// read-modify-write conflicts when there are many concurrent-writers to the same resource.\n161: \tPatch(orig config.Config, patchFn config.PatchFunc) (string, error)\n162: \n163: \t// Delete removes an object from the store by key\n164: \t// For k8s, resourceVersion must be fulfilled before a deletion is carried out.\n165: \t// If not possible, a 409 Conflict status will be returned.\n166: \tDelete(typ config.GroupVersionKind, name, namespace string, resourceVersion *string) error\n167: }\n168: \n169: type EventHandler = func(config.Config, config.Config, Event)\n170: \n171: // ConfigStoreCache is a local fully-replicated cache of the config store.  The\n172: // cache actively synchronizes its local state with the remote store and\n173: // provides a notification mechanism to receive update events. As such, the\n174: // notification handlers must be registered prior to calling _Run_, and the\n175: // cache requires initial synchronization grace period after calling  _Run_.\n176: //\n177: // Update notifications require the following consistency guarantee: the view\n178: // in the cache must be AT LEAST as fresh as the moment notification arrives, but\n179: // MAY BE more fresh (e.g. if _Delete_ cancels an _Add_ event).\n180: //\n181: // Handlers execute on the single worker queue in the order they are appended.\n182: // Handlers receive the notification event and the associated object. DestinationRule Merging Loses Metadata Identity\n\n**File:** `pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go:38-109`\n\nThe `mergeDestinationRule()` function merges multiple DRs for the same FQDN host into a single consolidated rule:\n\n```go\nfunc (ps *PushContext) mergeDestinationRule(p *consolidatedDestRules, destRuleConfig config.Config, exportToMap map[visibility.Instance]bool) {\n    rule := destRuleConfig.Spec.(*networking.DestinationRule)\n    resolvedHost := ResolveShortnameToFQDN(rule.Host, destRuleConfig.Meta)\n\n    if mdrList, exists := p.destRules[resolvedHost]; exists {\n        // ... matching logic ...\n        for i, mdr := range mdrList {\n            // Line 65-66: Deep copy and update existing rule in place\n            copied := mdr.DeepCopy()\n            p.destRules[resolvedHost][i] = &copied\n            mergedRule := copied.Spec.(*networking.DestinationRule)\n\n            // Lines 77-87: Merge subsets from new rule into existing rule\n            for _, subset := range rule.Subsets {\n                // append subsets to existing rule\n                mergedRule.Subsets = append(mergedRule.Subsets, subset)\n            }\n\n            // Lines 91-93: Merge traffic policy if not present\n            if mergedRule.TrafficPolicy == nil && rule.TrafficPolicy != nil {\n                mergedRule.TrafficPolicy = rule.TrafficPolicy\n            }\n        }\n        if addRuleToProcessedDestRules {\n            // New rule is added to list\n            p.destRules[resolvedHost] = append(p.destRules[resolvedHost], &destRuleConfig)\n        }\n        return\n    }\n\n    // First rule is simply added\n    p.destRules[resolvedHost] = append(p.destRules[resolvedHost], &destRuleConfig)\n}\n```\n\n**Critical Issue:** When two DRs are merged:\n- The first DR's config metadata (Name=\"reviews-traffic-policy\", Namespace=\"default\") is preserved\n- The second DR's metadata (Name=\"reviews-subsets\", Namespace=\"default\") is lost—only its Spec (subsets, traffic policy) is merged into the first DR's config\n- `p.destRules[resolvedHost]` contains only ONE config.Config element after merging, with the first DR's metadata\n\n### 2. // LINE 64: Calls DependsOnConfig with the updated DR's ConfigKey\n        if proxy.SidecarScope.DependsOnConfig(config) {\n            return true\n        }\n        // ...\n    }\n    return false\n}\n```\n\n**File:** `pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go:523-540` (in `DependsOnConfig()`)\n\n```go\nfunc (sc *SidecarScope) DependsOnConfig(config ConfigKey) bool {\n    if sc == nil {\n        return sc.configDependencies[config.HashCode()]\n    return exists\n}\n```\n\n**Critical Issue:** When a DestinationRule update event occurs:\n1. The event contains the ConfigKey for the updated DR: `{Kind: DestinationRule, Name: \"reviews-subsets\", Namespace: \"default\"}`\n2. This ConfigKey's hash is computed (lines 60-74 in `pilot/pkg/model/config.go`)\n3. `DependsOnConfig()` checks if this hash exists in `configDependencies`\n4. Since only \"reviews-traffic-policy\" was registered, the hash for \"reviews-subsets\" is NOT in the map\n5. `DependsOnConfig()` returns `false`\n6. The xDS push is SKIPPED\n\n### 5. Hash Computation\n\n**File:** `pilot/pkg/model/config.go:60-74`\n\n```go\nfunc (key ConfigKey) HashCode() uint64 {\n    hash := md5.New()\n    for _, v := range []string{\n        key.Name,\n        key.Namespace,\n        key.Kind.Kind,\n        key.Kind.Group,\n        key.Kind.Version,\n    } {\n        hash.Write([]byte(v))\n    }\n    var tmp [md5.Size]byte\n    sum := hash.Sum(tmp[:0])\n    return binary.BigEndian.Uint64(sum)\n}\n```\n\nThe hash includes the DR's Name, so:\n- \"reviews-traffic-policy\" → hash H1 (registered)\n- \"reviews-subsets\" → hash H2 (NOT registered)\n\nWhen \"reviews-subsets\" is updated, its ConfigKey generates hash H2, which is not in `configDependencies`, so the push is rejected.\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **`pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go`**\n   - `mergeDestinationRule()` - loses DR identity during merge\n\n2. **`pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go`**\n   - `DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace()` - only registers one DR's ConfigKey\n   - `ConvertToSidecarScope()` - only registers one DR's ConfigKey\n   - `AddConfigDependencies()` - called with incomplete list of DRs\n   - `DependsOnConfig()` - correctly checks dependencies but only has one DR's key\n\n3. **`pilot/pkg/xds/proxy_dependencies.go`**\n   - `ConfigAffectsProxy()` - correctly filters based on dependencies\n   - `checkProxyDependencies()` - correctly checks if proxy depends on config\n\n4. **`pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go`**\n   - `destinationRule()` - returns merged DRs with only one metadata\n   - `consolidatedDestRules` - stores only one config.Config per host\n   - `destinationRuleIndex` - stores consolidated rules without tracking all contributors\n\n5. **`pilot/pkg/model/config.go`**\n   - `ConfigKey.HashCode()` - correctly hashes individual keys, but only some keys are registered\n\n## Causal Chain\n\n1. **Symptom**: Operator updates `reviews-subsets` DR → Envoy sidecar receives no xDS update\n2. **Event Propagation**: Istio control plane detects the DestinationRule update event\n3. **Push Filtering (FAILURE POINT)**: `ConfigAffectsProxy()` is called with ConfigKey{Name: \"reviews-subsets\", ...}\n4. **Dependency Check**: `DependsOnConfig()` is called, which checks if hash of \"reviews-subsets\" is in `configDependencies`\n5. **Missing Dependency**: The hash for \"reviews-subsets\" is NOT found (only \"reviews-traffic-policy\" was registered)\n6. **Push Rejected**: `ConfigAffectsProxy()` returns `false`, push is skipped\n7. **Root Cause - Incomplete Registration**: Only \"reviews-traffic-policy\"'s ConfigKey was added to dependencies because:\n   - `DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace()` or `ConvertToSidecarScope()` called `ps.destinationRule()` which returned the merged DR\n   - The merged DR list contained only ONE config.Config (with \"reviews-traffic-policy\" metadata)\n   - Only one ConfigKey was registered via `AddConfigDependencies()`\n8. **Root Cause - Merging**: Only one DR's metadata survived the merge because:\n   - When `mergeDestinationRule()` processed the second DR, it merged its Spec into the first DR's config\n   - It never added a second config.Config to the `destRules[host]` list (unless workload selectors required it)\n   - The second DR's metadata was discarded\n\n## Diagnostic Steps\n\nTo verify this root cause in a live cluster:\n\n1. **Inspect the merged DR list:**\n   ```bash\n   kubectl port-forward -n istio-system <istiod-pod> 8080:8080\n   curl http://localhost:8080/debug/configz | jq '.destinationRules'\n   ```\n   Check that only ONE DR's Name/Namespace appears per host, despite multiple DRs being defined.\n\n2. **Inspect the SidecarScope dependencies:**\n   ```bash\n   curl http://localhost:8080/debug/configz | jq '.sidecarScopes[].configDependencies'\n   ```\n   Verify that only one DestinationRule ConfigKey is registered.\n\n3. **Trace the update event:**\n   Enable debug logging in Istiod and watch for:\n   - The DestinationRule update event being received\n   - `ConfigAffectsProxy()` being called with the updated DR's ConfigKey\n   - `DependsOnConfig()` returning `false` (no push triggered)\n\n4. **Compare with a single DR:**\n   Define only one DestinationRule per host and verify that updates DO trigger xDS pushes.\n\n## Recommendation\n\n**Fix Strategy:**\n\nThe solution requires registering ALL contributing DestinationRules in the SidecarScope dependencies, not just the one whose metadata survives the merge.\n\n### Option 1: Track Contributing DRs During Merge (Preferred)\n- Modify `consolidatedDestRules` to maintain a list of contributing DR ConfigKeys alongside the merged config\n- When creating SidecarScope dependencies, iterate over ALL contributing DRs, not just the merged result\n- **Impact**: Preserves the current merging behavior while fixing dependency tracking\n\n### Option 2: Store All DRs Without Merging Metadata\n- Modify `consolidatedDestRules.destRules` to keep multiple config.Config entries (one per source DR)\n- Only merge the Spec (subsets, traffic policy) into the first DR's config\n- Preserve each original DR's metadata separately\n- **Impact**: Requires changes to how merged DRs are retrieved by consumers\n\n### Option 3: Separate Merging from Dependency Tracking\n- Create a mapping from merged DR ConfigKey to all contributing DR ConfigKeys\n- When checking dependencies, include both direct matches and merged-into matches\n- **Impact**: Requires cross-referencing in the dependency lookup path\n\n**Minimal Necessary Fix:**\n1. In `consolidatedDestRules`, add a field: `contributingDRs map[host.Name][]ConfigKey` to track all contributing DR identities\n2. In `mergeDestinationRule()`, append each source DR's ConfigKey to the contributing list\n3. In `DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace()` and `ConvertToSidecarScope()`, iterate over contributing DRs instead of just the merged result\n4. Update `DependsOnConfig()` or the push filter to recognize that a proxy depends on a DR if it depends on any merged variant of that DR\n\nThis ensures that when ANY contributing DR is updated, the proxy receives the push.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":6,"cache_creation_input_tokens":6738,"cache_read_input_tokens":82051,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":6738},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"4f618fcd-3351-4045-9ccc-1defd1fcb716","uuid":"85967775-c72b-48d7-9f9d-1080ac0f8a3a"}

Hash Computation\n\n**File:** `pilot/pkg/model/config.go:60-74`\n\n```go\nfunc (key ConfigKey) HashCode() uint64 {\n    hash := md5.New()\n    for _, v := range []string{\n        key.Name,\n        key.Namespace,\n        key.Kind.Kind,\n        key.Kind.Group,\n        key.Kind.Version,\n    } {\n        hash.Write([]byte(v))\n    }\n    var tmp [md5.Size]byte\n    sum := hash.Sum(tmp[:0])\n    return binary.BigEndian.Uint64(sum)\n}\n```\n\nThe hash includes the DR's Name, so:\n- \"reviews-traffic-policy\" → hash H1 (registered)\n- \"reviews-subsets\" → hash H2 (NOT registered)\n\nWhen \"reviews-subsets\" is updated, its ConfigKey generates hash H2, which is not in `configDependencies`, so the push is rejected.\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **`pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go`**\n   - `mergeDestinationRule()` - loses DR identity during merge\n\n2. **`pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go`**\n   - `DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace()` - only registers one DR's ConfigKey\n   - `ConvertToSidecarScope()` - only registers one DR's ConfigKey\n   - `AddConfigDependencies()` - called with incomplete list of DRs\n   - `DependsOnConfig()` - correctly checks dependencies but only has one DR's key\n\n3. **`pilot/pkg/xds/proxy_dependencies.go`**\n   - `ConfigAffectsProxy()` - correctly filters based on dependencies\n   - `checkProxyDependencies()` - correctly checks if proxy depends on config\n\n4. **`pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go`**\n   - `destinationRule()` - returns merged DRs with only one metadata\n   - `consolidatedDestRules` - stores only one config.Config per host\n   - `destinationRuleIndex` - stores consolidated rules without tracking all contributors\n\n5. **`pilot/pkg/model/config.go`**\n   - `ConfigKey.HashCode()` - correctly hashes individual keys, but only some keys are registered\n\n## Causal Chain\n\n1. **Symptom**: Operator updates `reviews-subsets` DR → Envoy sidecar receives no xDS update\n2. **Event Propagation**: Istio control plane detects the DestinationRule update event\n3. **Push Filtering (FAILURE POINT)**: `ConfigAffectsProxy()` is called with ConfigKey{Name: \"reviews-subsets\", ...}\n4. **Dependency Check**: `DependsOnConfig()` is called, which checks if hash of \"reviews-subsets\" is in `configDependencies`\n5. **Missing Dependency**: The hash for \"reviews-subsets\" is NOT found (only \"reviews-traffic-policy\" was registered)\n6. **Push Rejected**: `ConfigAffectsProxy()` returns `false`, push is skipped\n7. **Root Cause - Incomplete Registration**: Only \"reviews-traffic-policy\"'s ConfigKey was added to dependencies because:\n   - `DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace()` or `ConvertToSidecarScope()` called `ps.destinationRule()` which returned the merged DR\n   - The merged DR list contained only ONE config.Config (with \"reviews-traffic-policy\" metadata)\n   - Only one ConfigKey was registered via `AddConfigDependencies()`\n8. **Root Cause - Merging**: Only one DR's metadata survived the merge because:\n   - When `mergeDestinationRule()` processed the second DR, it merged its Spec into the first DR's config\n   - It never added a second config.Config to the `destRules[host]` list (unless workload selectors required it)\n   - The second DR's metadata was discarded\n\n## Diagnostic Steps\n\nTo verify this root cause in a live cluster:\n\n1. **Inspect the merged DR list:**\n   ```bash\n   kubectl port-forward -n istio-system <istiod-pod> 8080:8080\n   curl http://localhost:8080/debug/configz | jq '.destinationRules'\n   ```\n   Check that only ONE DR's Name/Namespace appears per host, despite multiple DRs being defined.\n\n2. **Inspect the SidecarScope dependencies:**\n   ```bash\n   curl http://localhost:8080/debug/configz | jq '.sidecarScopes[].configDependencies'\n   ```\n   Verify that only one DestinationRule ConfigKey is registered.\n\n3. **Trace the update event:**\n   Enable debug logging in Istiod and watch for:\n   - The DestinationRule update event being received\n   - `ConfigAffectsProxy()` being called with the updated DR's ConfigKey\n   - `DependsOnConfig()` returning `false` (no push triggered)\n\n4. **Compare with a single DR:**\n   Define only one DestinationRule per host and verify that updates DO trigger xDS pushes.\n\n## Recommendation\n\n**Fix Strategy:**\n\nThe solution requires registering ALL contributing DestinationRules in the SidecarScope dependencies, not just the one whose metadata survives the merge.\n\n### Option 1: Track Contributing DRs During Merge (Preferred)\n- Modify `consolidatedDestRules` to maintain a list of contributing DR ConfigKeys alongside the merged config\n- When creating SidecarScope dependencies, iterate over ALL contributing DRs, not just the merged result\n- **Impact**: Preserves the current merging behavior while fixing dependency tracking\n\n### Option 2: Store All DRs Without Merging Metadata\n- Modify `consolidatedDestRules.destRules` to keep multiple config.Config entries (one per source DR)\n- Only merge the Spec (subsets, traffic policy) into the first DR's config\n- Preserve each original DR's metadata separately\n- **Impact**: Requires changes to how merged DRs are retrieved by consumers\n\n### Option 3: Separate Merging from Dependency Tracking\n- Create a mapping from merged DR ConfigKey to all contributing DR ConfigKeys\n- When checking dependencies, include both direct matches and merged-into matches\n- **Impact**: Requires cross-referencing in the dependency lookup path\n\n**Minimal Necessary Fix:**\n1. In `consolidatedDestRules`, add a field: `contributingDRs map[host.Name][]ConfigKey` to track all contributing DR identities\n2. In `mergeDestinationRule()`, append each source DR's ConfigKey to the contributing list\n3. In `DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace()` and `ConvertToSidecarScope()`, iterate over contributing DRs instead of just the merged result\n4. Update `DependsOnConfig()` or the push filter to recognize that a proxy depends on a DR if it depends on any merged variant of that DR\n\nThis ensures that when ANY contributing DR is updated, the proxy receives the push.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
